+# Spec — task_019: regrettable-content guard (secrets/PII pre-commit + pre-push block + pre-publish audit)
+
+## Task summary
+
+vibe containers commit and push freely under `bypassPermissions`, and in practice have committed personal/inappropriate content — PII, private-machine specifics, and even sensitive detail in commit *messages* — that made Time&I's Private→Public flip painful. Build a **vibe-core** guard that stops regrettable content leaving the machine: a git-hook layer (pre-commit + commit-msg + pre-push) that scans staged content AND commit messages AND the outgoing push range, blocking high-precision secrets and warning on lower-precision PII, with an explicit logged override; plus a host-side `vibe audit` command that scans a repo's **full history** for the Private→Public case a forward-looking hook cannot retroactively cover. It ships to every container via `install-claude-extras.sh` and must not false-positive on vibe's own repo (which deliberately contains example PII in its hygiene docs), on the mandatory `Co-Authored-By` commit trailer, or on intentionally-private repos (e.g. a brain2 knowledge base committed by its gardener).
+
+## Design (locked with Martin — not open for re-litigation)
+
+- **Two-tier response, block-by-default:** BLOCK on high-precision secrets; WARN on lower-precision PII. **Both tiers exit non-zero (block) by default** in the non-interactive agent context — the tier is a *confidence/severity label*, not a hard-vs-soft gate (see § WARN semantics). Override bypasses either.
+- **Ships core** — installed for every container, not user-specific.
+- **Self-contained** — pure POSIX/bash + grep ERE, no `gitleaks`/`trufflehog` (not in the firewall allowlist).
+- **Scans commit messages** for secrets, not just diffs (with trailer handling, see below).
+
+## Scanner contract (pinned, so Generator and Tester cannot guess differently)
+
+- **Invocation:** `vibe-content-scan.sh <mode>` where mode is `--staged` | `--message <file>` | `--range <a> <b>` | `--blob-stdin` (raw content on stdin, used by `vibe audit`).
+- **Output line format (one per finding), machine-parseable, tab-separated:**
+  `<CLASS>\t<location>\t<rule>\t<snippet>` — CLASS is the literal token `BLOCK` or `WARN`; location is `file:line` (or `message` / `commit <sha>` for non-file sources); rule is a short rule id (e.g. `github-pat`, `rfc1918-ip`); snippet is the matched substring, truncated to 60 chars. All findings go to stderr; stdout stays empty.
+- **Exit codes:** `0` = clean (or all findings suppressed/overridden); `1` = at least one un-suppressed finding that blocks. **Exit 1, not 2** — 2 is guard-bash.sh's PreToolUse protocol signal and is deliberately not reused here (git only cares zero vs non-zero).
+- **Tier scanning by mode:** `--staged` and `--message` scan **both** tiers. `--range` (pre-push backstop) scans **BLOCK tier only** for file content — rationale: PII already committed was seen by the commit-time gate, so re-flagging it on every push of the same branch is the "cries wolf" failure; pre-push exists to catch *secrets* that reach the push range by any route. `vibe audit --history` scans **both** tiers for file content — it is a one-shot, deliberately-invoked scan with no repeat-nag problem, and WARN-tier PII sitting in history is exactly what a Private→Public flip needs surfaced. Every mode that scans commit messages scans both tiers against those messages (subject to the trailer exemption below).
+- **Built-in default allowlist (scanner-level, applies to EVERY repo, not opt-in):** the scanner always suppresses (a) the `Co-Authored-By:` / `Signed-off-by:` git trailer lines and the literal address `noreply@anthropic.com` and `*.users.noreply.github.com`; (b) email/IP findings on lines matching a standard git trailer (`^[A-Z][A-Za-z-]+:\s`). This is what stops the guard firing on its own commit convention.
+- **Message-tier email rule:** the WARN email rule, when scanning a commit *message*, ignores trailer lines per the built-in allowlist above; it still catches a raw address pasted into free-text message body.
+
+## WARN semantics (resolves the non-TTY ambiguity)
+
+Commits here are made by Claude via the Bash tool with no TTY, so an interactive "confirm y/n" is impossible. Therefore: **both BLOCK and WARN exit non-zero by default** and both are cleared the same way (allowlist entry, opt-out marker, or `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off`). The tier distinction is real but narrow: (1) WARN findings are labelled `WARN` in output and grouped separately in `vibe audit`; (2) a repo can globally silence a whole WARN *class* via config without silencing BLOCK; (3) BLOCK denotes near-certain secrets a human should almost never override, WARN denotes probable PII a human often legitimately keeps (via allowlist). The spec does NOT claim WARN is a softer runtime gate in the agent context — it is not.
+
+## Components (target shape; Generator may refine mechanics, not remove capability)
+
+1. `devcontainer/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh` — the single scanner core implementing the § Scanner contract.
+2. `devcontainer/git-hooks/pre-commit`, `commit-msg`, `pre-push` — thin wrappers translating git's real hook contract into scanner modes:
+   - `pre-commit` → `--staged`.
+   - `commit-msg` → `--message "$1"` ($1 is the message-file path git passes).
+   - `pre-push` → reads stdin lines `<localref> <localsha> <remoteref> <remotesha>`; **per line: if `<localsha>` is all-zeros (branch delete) → skip (nothing to scan); if `<remotesha>` is all-zeros (new branch) → scan commits reachable from localsha but not from any existing remote ref (`git rev-list <localsha> --not --remotes`); else → scan `<remotesha>..<localsha>`.** Empty range → exit 0. (`--not --remotes` scopes across all configured remotes; correct for vibe's one-remote-per-container model. A rare multi-remote first-push to a second remote could under-scan commits already tracked via another remote — accepted limitation, not covered by an AC.)
+3. `install-claude-extras.sh`: new `install_git_hooks()` — copy the hooks dir to `${CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR:-$HOME/.claude}/vibe-git-hooks/` (chmod +x on the three wrappers + scanner) and set `git config --global core.hooksPath` to that dir inside the container. Idempotent; added to the existing `install_*` call list.
+4. **Per-repo opt-out (single syntax):** a repo-root marker file `.vibe-content-guard-off`. When present, the scanner exits `0` immediately. This exempts an intentionally-private repo whose commits happen *in-container* — the brain2 **gardener** (whose `/workspace` is the brain2 repo and which commits in-container) is the flagship case; reader containers never commit brain2 so are irrelevant here. Absence = guarded (block-by-default).
+5. **Override (per-invocation, logged):** `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` in the environment bypasses the scan for that one git invocation and prints a loud stderr line naming what was skipped (rule ids). git-native `git commit --no-verify` / `git push --no-verify` also bypass and are documented. Never silent. `VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1` is accepted as an alias.
+6. **Allowlist (precise semantics):** a repo-root `.vibe-content-allow` file — one **ERE regex per line**, `#` comments and blank lines ignored, case-sensitive. A finding is suppressed iff its **whole flagged line** matches (`grep -E`) any allow entry. vibe's own repo ships a `.vibe-content-allow` covering **doc/fragment literals only**: the hygiene-doc example PII (`/Users/martin`, the example IPs, `mcomz.local`/`pi02.local`) and the SECURITY.md maintainer link — so criterion 6 holds. Test fixtures need no allowlist entry: they are runtime-constructed and never staged as literals (§ Dogfooding).
+7. `vibe audit [--history|--staged]` (host-side subcommand in the `vibe` launcher, dispatched like `vibe repos`, before `parse_vibe_args`) — `--history` (default) scans the **full history, BOTH tiers**: all added content across every commit via `git log -p --all` piped through the scanner (`--blob-stdin`), plus every commit message (`git log --all --format=%B`). This catches both a secret and PII (IP/personal-path/`.local`) committed then later deleted — the exact Private→Public case. In `--blob-stdin` audit mode the scanner **tracks the most recent `commit <sha>` header** in the `git log -p` stream and attributes each finding's location to that commit (location = `commit <sha>`), so a human knows where to look. Findings grouped by class (BLOCK then WARN); exit `1` if any BLOCK-class finding, `0` otherwise (WARN-only history exits `0` but still lists the WARN findings — advisory for the flip). `--staged` runs the pre-commit-equivalent scan on demand. Respects `.vibe-content-allow`.
+8. `devcontainer/claude-md/content-guard.md` — managed fragment teaching in-container Claude: the two tiers, the `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` override, the `.vibe-content-allow`/`.vibe-content-guard-off` files, and `vibe audit` (mirrors `learn-hook.md`).
+9. Docs/tests: `smoke-test.py` `test_task019_*` cases for every AC; a `MANUAL-TESTS.md` section; a `CHANGELOG.md` entry in the same commit; a README mention.
+
+## Dogfooding (how this task lands without fighting its own guard)
+
+Test fixtures must never commit a *literal* real-shaped secret into vibe's repo. Two rules: (1) smoke-test fixtures **construct** bad strings at runtime by concatenation (e.g. `"ghp_" + "A"*36`, `"-----BEGIN " + "OPENSSH PRIVATE KEY-----"`) and write them into throwaway temp repos — so no contiguous secret pattern is ever staged in vibe's own tree; (2) for any unavoidable literal (illustrative strings in docs/fragment), add a matching `.vibe-content-allow` entry. The landing commit of this task may additionally use `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` if needed, but rule (1) should make that unnecessary.
+
+## Detection rules
+
+**BLOCK tier (high-precision secrets):**
+- GitHub PAT: `ghp_[A-Za-z0-9]{36}`, `github_pat_[A-Za-z0-9_]{22,}`.
+- OpenAI/Anthropic-style: `sk-[A-Za-z0-9-]{20,}`.
+- AWS access key id: `AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}`.
+- Private key blocks: `-----BEGIN ([A-Z ]+ )?PRIVATE KEY-----`.
+- Secret-named assignment: a key matching `(?i)(secret|token|password|passwd|api[_-]?key|bearer)` assigned (`=`/`:`) a value of ≥16 chars from `[A-Za-z0-9+/=_-]`. (Test fixtures for this rule are runtime-constructed per § Dogfooding.)
+
+**WARN tier (lower-precision PII, source list = `devcontainer/claude-md/project-hygiene.md`):**
+- RFC1918 / link-local IPs: `10.`, `172.(1[6-9]|2[0-9]|3[01]).`, `192.168.`, `169.254.` octet patterns.
+- Personal home paths: `/Users/[^/ ]+/`, `/home/[^/ ]+/` — **excluding** the generic container users `node` and `root`.
+- `.local` mDNS hostnames: `[A-Za-z0-9-]+\.local\b`.
+- Email addresses: `[A-Za-z0-9._%+-]+@[A-Za-z0-9.-]+\.[A-Za-z]{2,}` — with the trailer/noreply exemptions from § Scanner contract.
+
+## Acceptance criteria (mechanical — each verifiable by a smoke-test; fixtures runtime-constructed per § Dogfooding)
+
+1. `vibe-content-scan.sh --staged` in a temp repo whose staged diff adds a runtime-built `ghp_`+36-char token exits `1` and emits a `BLOCK` line naming rule `github-pat`.
+2. `vibe-content-scan.sh --message <file>` where the file contains a runtime-built OpenSSH "BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY" block marker (the real contiguous form, constructed at test time) exits `1` with a `BLOCK` line (message tier scans secrets).
+3. `vibe-content-scan.sh --staged` on a diff adding `[redacted-ip]`, no allowlist/override, exits `1` AND emits a `WARN` line (class token distinct from `BLOCK`) naming rule `rfc1918-ip`.
+4. `vibe-content-scan.sh --staged` on a clean diff (ordinary code) exits `0` with no findings.
+5. With `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off`, the AC1 scan exits `0` AND prints a stderr line naming the bypass and the skipped rule(s).
+6. **(mechanism, synthetic)** A temp repo with a `.vibe-content-allow` entry whose regex matches the flagged line → that finding is suppressed; a scan whose only finding is allow-listed exits `0`. A second temp repo without the entry → same content exits `1`. (No coupling to live doc text.)
+7. A repo-root `.vibe-content-guard-off` marker makes the scanner exit `0` immediately even on AC1 BLOCK content.
+8. Running the real `install-claude-extras.sh` against an isolated `HOME`/`CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR`/`GIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL` installs the scanner + three wrappers executable under `<cfg>/vibe-git-hooks/`, and afterwards `git config --global core.hooksPath` actually returns that path (real config state, not a stubbed call capture).
+9. `vibe audit --history` on a throwaway repo whose HISTORY contains a runtime-built `ghp_` token that was committed and then **deleted** in a later commit exits `1` and reports the finding as a `BLOCK` line whose location names the specific commit sha (full-history, not HEAD-only); a clean-history repo exits `0`.
+10. **(integration, end-to-end through the installed hooks)** In a throwaway `git init` repo with a local bare remote and `core.hooksPath` pointed at the installed dir: a real `git commit` of clean content succeeds and a real `git commit` of AC1 BLOCK content fails via the actual `pre-commit` wrapper; a real `git push` of a **new branch** whose tip commit added a secret fails via the actual `pre-push` wrapper (exercises the zero-SHA new-branch range rule).
+11. A real Claude-style commit **message** ending `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>` scans **clean** (exit `0`) through `--message` — the built-in trailer exemption holds (guards concern 1: the guard must not fire on its own convention).
+12. The pre-existing `guard-bash.sh` force-push block still fires unchanged (`git push --force` without lease → exit 2) — no regression.
+13. `python3 code-check.py` (shellcheck) clean across all shell files including the new scanner + hooks.
+14. `python3 smoke-test.py` — full pre-existing suite still green (no regressions).
+15. A managed fragment `devcontainer/claude-md/content-guard.md` exists naming: the two tiers, the `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` override, the `.vibe-content-allow`/`.vibe-content-guard-off` files, and `vibe audit`.
+16. `vibe audit --history` on a throwaway repo whose history has an RFC1918 IP (`[redacted-ip]`) in a file committed then later deleted → the WARN finding is **reported** in the audit output (a `WARN` line whose location names the commit) even though exit is `0` (WARN-only history is advisory, not blocking). Proves audit surfaces **both** tiers in history, not just secrets.
+17. A commit whose only finding is WARN-tier file content (an RFC1918 IP), landed with `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` at commit time, then pushed as a new branch through the real installed `pre-push` wrapper → `git push` **succeeds** with no override (pre-push scans BLOCK-tier only for file content, so already-committed WARN PII does not re-block). Proves the pre-push "cries wolf" fix holds.
+
+## Out of scope (do NOT build)
+
+- Git **history rewriting** / `filter-repo` / BFG. `vibe audit` only *reports*; never rewrites (destructive, separate deliberate op).
+- External scanners (`gitleaks`/`trufflehog`) or any new network dependency.
+- Full Shannon-entropy detection (only the simple secret-named-assignment heuristic in v1).
+- Changing `guard-bash.sh`/`guard-fs.sh`/firewall behaviour beyond composing (AC12 guards this).
+- Per-project OpenProject gating (separate finding → TODO, not this task).
+- Auto-fixing/redacting flagged content — the guard blocks/warns and reports; the human decides.
+- Persisting an override against a specific commit SHA so pre-push doesn't re-scan (avoided instead by pre-push scanning secrets-only — see § Scanner contract).
+
+## Note on `core.hooksPath` global scope (concern 14)
+
+`core.hooksPath` is set `--global` in-container, so it also covers rw `/repos/*` shared repos and (in the gardener) brain2. This is intended — a shared repo may also go public, so guarding it is correct; an intentionally-private one uses `.vibe-content-guard-off`. No interaction with task_017 credential routing (hooks read content, never credentials).
+
+## Test location
+
+`smoke-test.py` — new `test_task019_*` functions (host-side; subprocess-invoke the scanner, install script, and real git hooks against crafted temp repos with runtime-built fixtures; assert exit codes + output tokens), matching the existing `test_task0NN_*` convention. Tester-only and immutable once written. Shellcheck via `code-check.py`.
+
+## Proposed budget
+
+**3 cycles.** C1: scanner core + three wrappers + install wiring + fragment + allowlist/opt-out/override + built-in trailer exemption (ACs 1-8,10-13,15,17). C2: `vibe audit` launcher subcommand + full-history both-tier scan (ACs 9,16). C3: contingency for regressions/AC14 + docs (README, MANUAL-TESTS, CHANGELOG). Fewer if C1 lands broad.
+
+## Model plan
+
+- Planner + Evaluator: session model (Opus chair).
+- Spec Critic: sonnet.
+- Generator: **sonnet**, ceiling **opus** (security-adjacent shell + regex correctness — escalate on a capability-fail, not on spec/test issues).
+- Tester: haiku, → sonnet only if test *quality* is flagged.
+- **Fable rung: NOT pre-authorised** (Fable rationing 2026-07-11; no credit spend without a fresh ask). Well-specified — Sonnet-appropriate.
+
+## Invariants (from CLAUDE.md — must hold)
+
+- Don't weaken the firewall or the existing guard hooks (compose only; AC12).
+- Every PAT stays single-repo; no change to credential routing.
+- Self-contained; must **not** block normal commits in ordinary use — the built-in trailer exemption (AC11), allowlist, opt-out, and pre-push-secrets-only design are what protect this. A guard that cries wolf gets disabled.

+## 2026-07-15
+
+- [x] **regrettable-content guard: secrets/PII pre-commit + pre-push block + pre-publish audit (task_019)** — vibe containers commit and push freely under `bypassPermissions`, and in practice that has landed personal/private-machine PII, and even the odd secret, in a repo before anyone noticed — the exact pain the Time&I Private→Public flip surfaced. New self-contained (POSIX/bash + grep ERE only, no `gitleaks`/`trufflehog`, no network) scanner core `devcontainer/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh` implements four modes pinned by `.vs/spec.md`'s Scanner contract — `--staged`, `--message <file>`, `--range <a> <b>`, `--blob-stdin [--tier block]` — emitting tab-separated `<CLASS>\t<location>\t<rule>\t<snippet>` findings to stderr (stdout always empty), exit `1` on any un-suppressed finding, never `2` (reserved for `guard-bash.sh`'s PreToolUse protocol). Two severities, both exit non-zero by default since these commits run non-interactively with no TTY for a y/n prompt: **BLOCK** (GitHub PATs, OpenAI/Anthropic-style keys, AWS access keys, private-key blocks, secret-shaped assignments) and **WARN** (RFC1918/link-local IPs, personal home paths excluding the generic `node`/`root` container users, `.local` mDNS hostnames, email addresses). A built-in allowlist needs no configuration — `Co-Authored-By:`/`Signed-off-by:` trailers and `noreply@anthropic.com`/`*.users.noreply.github.com` are always exempt, and email/IP findings are suppressed on any generic trailer-shaped line — so the guard never fires on its own commit convention (verified against a real Claude-style trailer). Three thin wrappers (`pre-commit` → `--staged`; `commit-msg` → `--message "$1"`; `pre-push` → the zero-SHA rules from spec component 2, scanning BLOCK-tier-only on the outgoing range so already-committed WARN-tier PII doesn't "cry wolf" on every push) translate git's real hook contract into scanner invocations. `install-claude-extras.sh` gains `install_git_hooks()` — copies the hooks dir to `${CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR:-$HOME/.claude}/vibe-git-hooks/`, chmod +x, sets `git config --global core.hooksPath` — idempotent, wired into the existing call list; Dockerfile gains the matching `COPY git-hooks/`. Two escape hatches, both loud, never silent: a per-invocation `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` (alias `VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1`) override that still runs the scan and names every skipped rule id on stderr; a per-repo `.vibe-content-guard-off` marker that exempts an intentionally-private repo entirely (the brain2 gardener is the flagship case — its `/workspace` IS brain2 and it commits in-container; `core.hooksPath` is deliberately `--global`, so it also covers rw `/repos/*` shared repos). A repo-root `.vibe-content-allow` (one ERE regex per line, `#`/blank ignored, case-sensitive, whole-flagged-line match) handles known deliberate literals; vibe's own repo ships one covering its hygiene-doc example PII (`/Users/martin`, the example IPs, `mcomz.local`/`pi02.local`) so the guard doesn't fire on its own documentation. New host-side `vibe audit [--history|--staged]` subcommand (dispatches like `vibe repos`, before `parse_vibe_args`, entirely host-side against the current directory's git repo — no container) covers what a forward-looking git-hook layer structurally cannot: `--history` scans the FULL history, both tiers — `git log -p --all` piped through `--blob-stdin` for content (which tracks `commit <sha>` headers itself, so every finding names the exact commit) plus every commit message individually re-attributed from `--message`'s generic `message` location to `commit <sha>` — catching a secret or an IP that was committed and later deleted, the exact Private→Public case. Exit `1` only on a BLOCK-class finding; WARN-only history exits `0` but still lists every WARN finding as advisory. Never rewrites history, only reports. Two implementation notes worth recording: (1) the scanner's diff-parsing helper had to move from a `cmd | function` pipe to process substitution (`function < <(cmd)`) partway through, since bash pipeline components run in subshells and were silently discarding the global finding-accumulator state; (2) `code-check.py`'s `scripts()` was deliberately left untouched (not extended to glob `devcontainer/git-hooks/`) after doing so broke a pre-existing Tester-immutable smoke fixture (`_patched_code_check`) that does a literal-string replace of `scripts()`'s exact source text — shellcheck cleanliness of the new hook scripts is verified directly instead (`shellcheck --shell=bash --severity=warning` on all four files, and manually via `python3 code-check.py` with the git-hooks directory temporarily wired in during development). MANUAL-TESTS gains Test 35 (six sub-cases, the one thing the host-side smoke suite structurally can't see: a live in-container `git commit`/`git push` actually routed through the installed hooks). New managed fragment `devcontainer/claude-md/content-guard.md` teaches every session the two tiers, the override, the allowlist/opt-out files, and `vibe audit`. shellcheck clean across all new shell files; full pre-existing smoke suite green, no regressions.

+# Regrettable-content guard (git hooks + `vibe audit`)
+
+Every vibe container ships a git-hook layer that scans content BEFORE it
+leaves the machine — staged diffs, commit messages, and outgoing pushes —
+for secrets and personal/private-machine PII. It composes with, and never
+replaces, `guard-bash.sh`'s force-push/branch-delete block.
+
+## Two tiers, both non-blocking-by-default only via explicit override
+
+- **BLOCK** — high-precision secrets: GitHub PATs, OpenAI/Anthropic-style
+  keys, AWS access key ids, private-key blocks, and a generic
+  secret/token/password/api-key-shaped assignment of a long value.
+- **WARN** — lower-precision PII: RFC1918/link-local IPs, personal home
+  paths (`/Users/<name>/`, `/home/<name>/` — excluding the generic
+  container users `node`/`root`), `.local` mDNS hostnames, and email
+  addresses.
+
+Because commits here run non-interactively via the Bash tool (no TTY for a
+y/n prompt), **both tiers exit non-zero by default** — WARN is not a softer
+runtime gate, it is a severity label. Both are cleared the same way: an
+allowlist entry, the opt-out marker, or the loud override below. `git commit
+--no-verify` / `git push --no-verify` also bypass, git-natively.
+
+`pre-commit` and `commit-msg` scan both tiers. `pre-push` re-scans only the
+BLOCK tier on the outgoing push range — PII already committed was already
+seen by the commit-time gate, so re-flagging it on every push of the same
+branch is the "cries wolf" failure that gets a guard disabled; pre-push
+exists to catch secrets that reach the push range by any other route.
+
+## Override: `VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off` (or `VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1`)
+
+Set either in the environment to bypass enforcement for that one git
+invocation. Never silent — the scanner prints a loud stderr line naming the
+override and every rule id it skipped. Prefer this over disabling the guard
+outright when a finding is a deliberate one-off (e.g. Martin's own IP in a
+throwaway test fixture that never gets committed for real).
+
+## Per-repo opt-out: `.vibe-content-guard-off`
+
+A repo-root marker file that makes the scanner exit clean immediately, no
+scanning at all. For a repo that's intentionally private end-to-end — the
+brain2 gardener (whose `/workspace` IS the brain2 repo and commits
+in-container) is the flagship case. Reader containers never commit brain2,
+so this never applies to them.
+
+## Per-repo allowlist: `.vibe-content-allow`
+
+A repo-root file, one ERE regex per line (`#` comments and blank lines
+ignored, case-sensitive). A finding is suppressed iff its **whole flagged
+line** matches any entry. Use this for known, deliberate literals — vibe's
+own repo ships one covering the example PII in its own hygiene docs
+(`/Users/martin`, the example IPs, `mcomz.local`/`pi02.local`) and the
+SECURITY.md maintainer link, so the guard never fires on its own
+documentation.
+
+The scanner also has a **built-in allowlist that needs no configuration**:
+`Co-Authored-By:`/`Signed-off-by:` trailer lines, `noreply@anthropic.com`,
+and `*.users.noreply.github.com` are always exempt — this is what stops the
+guard firing on its own commit convention.
+
+## `vibe audit [--history|--staged]`
+
+Host-side command (run from the project directory, like `vibe repos`) that
+scans **beyond** what the forward-looking git hooks can retroactively cover
+— the case a Private→Public repo flip actually needs. `--history` (default)
+scans the full history, both tiers, including content that was committed
+and later deleted: a secret or an IP that only ever existed for a few
+commits is still visible to a clone of the repo's history. Exits `1` only
+if a BLOCK-class finding turns up anywhere in history; WARN-only history
+exits `0` but still lists every WARN finding — advisory, for the human
+doing the flip to review. `--staged` runs the same check as `pre-commit`,
+on demand. `vibe audit` never rewrites history — it only reports; a real
+Private→Public flip needing history rewritten is a separate, deliberate
+operation (`git filter-repo` / BFG), never automated by this guard.

+#!/usr/bin/env bash
+# vibe commit-msg hook (task_019) — thin wrapper translating git's real
+# commit-msg contract ($1 = path to the message file) into the scanner's
+# --message mode. Installed alongside pre-commit/pre-push by
+# install-claude-extras.sh's install_git_hooks().
+#
+# Override without editing this file: VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off (or
+# VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1), or the git-native `git commit --no-verify`.
+set -euo pipefail
+
+HOOK_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd -P)"
+SCANNER="$HOOK_DIR/vibe-content-scan.sh"
+
+if [ ! -x "$SCANNER" ]; then
+  echo "vibe commit-msg: scanner not found at $SCANNER — skipping content guard" >&2
+  exit 0
+fi
+
+"$SCANNER" --message "$1"

+#

+# VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1), or the git-native `git commit --no-verify`.
+set -euo pipefail

@@ -0,0 +1,76 @@
+#!/usr/bin/env bash
+# vibe pre-push hook (task_019) — thin wrapper translating git's real
+# pre-push contract into the scanner's BLOCK-tier-only backstop.
+#
+# git passes remote name/URL as $1/$2 and feeds stdin lines of the form:
+#   <local ref> <local sha1> <remote ref> <remote sha1>
+#
+# Per line (§ Scanner contract / spec.md component 2):
+#   - local sha all-zeros   -> branch delete, nothing to scan.
+#   - remote sha all-zeros  -> new branch: scan commits reachable from
+#     local sha but not from any existing remote ref
+#     (`git rev-list <local> --not --remotes`), via --blob-stdin --tier block
+#     so multi-commit new-branch pushes get commit-sha-attributed findings.
+#   - otherwise             -> scan <remote sha>..<local sha> via --range,
+#     BLOCK tier only (already-committed WARN-tier PII was seen by the
+#     commit-time gate; re-flagging it on every push is the "cries wolf"
+#     failure pre-push exists to avoid — see spec.md § Scanner contract).
+#
+# Override without editing this file: VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off (or
+# VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1), or the git-native `git push --no-verify`.
+set -euo pipefail
+
+HOOK_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd -P)"
+SCANNER="$HOOK_DIR/vibe-content-scan.sh"
+
+if [ ! -x "$SCANNER" ]; then
+  echo "vibe pre-push: scanner not found at $SCANNER — skipping content guard" >&2
+  exit 0
+fi
+
+# is_zero_sha <sha> — true iff every character is '0' (SHA-1 or SHA-256,
+# any length — no hardcoded 40).
+is_zero_sha() {
+  case "$1" in
+    *[!0]*) return 1 ;;
+    "") return 1 ;;
+    *) return 0 ;;
+  esac
+}
+
+status=0
+
+# local_ref/remote_ref are part of git's stdin protocol and must be
+# consumed positionally even though only the two sha fields are used.
+# shellcheck disable=SC2034
+while read -r local_ref local_sha remote_ref remote_sha; do
+  [ -n "${local_sha:-}" ] || continue
+
+  if is_zero_sha "$local_sha"; then
+    continue  # branch delete - nothing to scan
+  fi
+
+  if is_zero_sha "$remote_sha"; then
+    # New branch: commits reachable from local_sha but not from any
+    # existing remote ref.
+    commits_raw="$(git rev-list "$local_sha" --not --remotes 2>/dev/null || true)"
+    [ -n "$commits_raw" ] || continue
+    commit_array=()
+    while IFS= read -r c; do
+      [ -n "$c" ] && commit_array+=("$c")
+    done <<< "$commits_raw"
+    [ "${#commit_array[@]}" -gt 0 ] || continue
+    if ! git log -p --no-color "${commit_array[@]}" 2>/dev/null \
+         | "$SCANNER" --blob-stdin --tier block; then
+      status=1
+    fi
+  else
+    count="$(git rev-list --count "$remote_sha..$local_sha" 2>/dev/null || echo 0)"
+    [ "$count" -gt 0 ] || continue
+    if ! "$SCANNER" --range "$remote_sha" "$local_sha"; then
+      status=1
+    fi
+  fi
+done
+
+exit "$status"
diff --git a/devcontainer/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh b/devcontainer/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh
new file mode 100755
index 0000000..ebc3c6a
--- /dev/null
+++ b/devcontainer/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh
@@ -0,0 +1,312 @@
+#!/usr/bin/env bash
+# vibe-content-scan.sh — task_019 regrettable-content guard.
+#
+# Self-contained POSIX/bash + grep ERE scanner for secrets (BLOCK tier) and
+# lower-precision PII (WARN tier). No network, no gitleaks/trufflehog.
+#
+# Invocation:
+#   vibe-content-scan.sh --staged
+#   vibe-content-scan.sh --message <file>
+#   vibe-content-scan.sh --range <a> <b>
+#   vibe-content-scan.sh --blob-stdin [--tier block]
+#
+# Output: one line per finding on STDERR, tab-separated:
+#   <CLASS>\t<location>\t<rule>\t<snippet>
+# CLASS is BLOCK or WARN. stdout is always empty.
+#
+# Exit codes: 0 = clean (or every finding suppressed/overridden); 1 = at
+# least one un-suppressed finding. Never 2 (that is guard-bash.sh's
+# PreToolUse protocol signal, deliberately not reused here).
+#
+# Overrides (both logged loudly, never silent):
+#   VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off   — skip enforcement for this invocation
+#   VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1      — alias for the same
+# Per-repo opt-out: a repo-root .vibe-content-guard-off marker file makes
+# this script exit 0 immediately, before any scanning.
+# Per-repo allowlist: a repo-root .vibe-content-allow file, one ERE regex
+# per line (# comments / blank lines ignored, case-sensitive); a finding is
+# suppressed iff its whole flagged line matches (grep -E) any entry.
+#
+# See .vs/spec.md (task_019) for the full pinned contract this implements,
+# and devcontainer/claude-md/content-guard.md for the in-session summary.
+
+set -euo pipefail
+
+# ── Repo root + per-repo opt-out ─────────────────────────────────────────────
+REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel 2>/dev/null || pwd -P)"
+
+if [ -f "$REPO_ROOT/.vibe-content-guard-off" ]; then
+  exit 0
+fi
+
+ALLOWLIST_FILE="$REPO_ROOT/.vibe-content-allow"
+
+# ── Override detection (does not skip scanning — still reports what would
+# have fired, then exits 0 with a loud stderr line naming the bypass). ──────
+GUARD_OVERRIDE=0
+if [ "${VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD:-}" = "off" ] || [ "${VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT:-}" = "1" ]; then
+  GUARD_OVERRIDE=1
+fi
+
+# ── Finding accumulators (global, mutated by scan_line/check_rule) ─────────
+FOUND=0
+declare -a FOUND_RULES=()
+
+# line_is_allowlisted <content> — true iff the whole line matches any ERE
+# in $ALLOWLIST_FILE (comments/blanks ignored, case-sensitive).
+line_is_allowlisted() {
+  local content="$1"
+  [ -f "$ALLOWLIST_FILE" ] || return 1
+  local pattern
+  while IFS= read -r pattern || [ -n "$pattern" ]; do
+    case "$pattern" in
+      ""|\#*) continue ;;
+    esac
+    if printf '%s' "$content" | grep -qE -- "$pattern" 2>/dev/null; then
+      return 0
+    fi
+  done < "$ALLOWLIST_FILE"
+  return 1
+}
+
+# record_rule <rule> — append to FOUND_RULES if not already present.
+record_rule() {
+  local rule="$1" r
+  for r in "${FOUND_RULES[@]}"; do
+    [ "$r" = "$rule" ] && return 0
+  done
+  FOUND_RULES+=("$rule")
+  return 0
+}
+
+# check_rule <class> <rule> <ere-pattern> <icase:0|1> <content> <location>
+# Emits a finding line to stderr (unless allowlisted) and marks FOUND=1.
+check_rule() {
+  local class="$1" rule="$2" pattern="$3" icase="$4" content="$5" location="$6"
+  local m
+  if [ "$icase" = "1" ]; then
+    m=$(printf '%s' "$content" | grep -oiE -- "$pattern" 2>/dev/null | head -n1) || true
+  else
+    m=$(printf '%s' "$content" | grep -oE -- "$pattern" 2>/dev/null | head -n1) || true
+  fi
+  [ -z "$m" ] && return 0
+
+  if line_is_allowlisted "$content"; then
+    return 0
+  fi
+
+  local snippet="${m:0:60}"
+  printf '%s\t%s\t%s\t%s\n' "$class" "$location" "$rule" "$snippet" >&2
+  FOUND=1
+  record_rule "$rule"
+}
+
+# is_named_trailer <content> — Co-Authored-By: / Signed-off-by: lines are
+# fully exempt from ALL rules (built-in allowlist (a)).
+is_named_trailer() {
+  printf '%s' "$1" | grep -qiE '^(Co-authored-by|Signed-off-by):[[:space:]]'
+}
+
+# is_trailer_line <content> — a generic git-trailer-shaped line
+# (^[A-Z][A-Za-z-]+:\s). Built-in allowlist (b): suppresses email/IP
+# findings specifically (not BLOCK findings) on lines shaped like this.
+is_trailer_line() {
+  printf '%s' "$1" | grep -qE '^[A-Za-z][A-Za-z-]+:[[:space:]]'
+}
+
+# is_noreply_email <matched-address> — the literal exemptions in the
+# built-in allowlist: noreply@anthropic.com and *@*.users.noreply.github.com.
+is_noreply_email() {
+  case "$1" in
+    noreply@anthropic.com) return 0 ;;
+    *@*.users.noreply.github.com) return 0 ;;
+    *) return 1 ;;
+  esac
+}
+
+# check_email_rule <content> <location> — WARN email rule with the
+# noreply/trailer exemptions applied inline (can't be expressed as a single
+# ERE, so it gets its own small function instead of going through check_rule).
+check_email_rule() {
+  local content="$1" location="$2"
+  is_trailer_line "$content" && return 0
+  local m
+  m=$(printf '%s' "$content" | grep -oE '[A-Za-z0-9._%+-]+@[A-Za-z0-9.-]+\.[A-Za-z]{2,}' 2>/dev/null | head -n1) || true
+  [ -z "$m" ] && return 0
+  is_noreply_email "$m" && return 0
+  if line_is_allowlisted "$content"; then
+    return 0
+  fi
+  local snippet="${m:0:60}"
+  printf '%s\t%s\t%s\t%s\n' "WARN" "$location" "email-address" "$snippet" >&2
+  FOUND=1
+  record_rule "email-address"
+}
+
+# check_home_path_rule <content> <location> — WARN home-path rule, excluding
+# the generic container users node/root.
+check_home_path_rule() {
+  local content="$1" location="$2"
+  local m user
+  m=$(printf '%s' "$content" | grep -oE '/(Users|home)/[^/ ]+/' 2>/dev/null | head -n1) || true
+  [ -z "$m" ] && return 0
+  user=$(printf '%s' "$m" | sed -E 's#^/(Users|home)/([^/]+)/#\2#')
+  case "$user" in
+    node|root) return 0 ;;
+  esac
+  if line_is_allowlisted "$content"; then
+    return 0
+  fi
+  local snippet="${m:0:60}"
+  printf '%s\t%s\t%s\t%s\n' "WARN" "$location" "home-path" "$snippet" >&2
+  FOUND=1
+  record_rule "home-path"
+}
+
+# check_ip_rule <content> <location> — WARN rfc1918-ip rule, suppressed on
+# trailer-shaped lines (built-in allowlist (b)).
+check_ip_rule() {
+  local content="$1" location="$2"
+  is_trailer_line "$content" && return 0
+  local pattern='(10\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}|172\.(1[6-9]|2[0-9]|3[01])\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}|192\.168\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}|169\.254\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3})'
+  check_rule "WARN" "rfc1918-ip" "$pattern" "0" "$content" "$location"
+}
+
+# scan_line <content> <location> <tier: both|block> — runs every applicable
+# rule against one line of content.
+scan_line() {
+  local content="$1" location="$2" tier="$3"
+
+  is_named_trailer "$content" && return 0
+
+  # BLOCK tier — always scanned regardless of mode.
+  check_rule "BLOCK" "github-pat" 'ghp_[A-Za-z0-9]{36}|github_pat_[A-Za-z0-9_]{22,}' "0" "$content" "$location"
+  check_rule "BLOCK" "openai-key" 'sk-[A-Za-z0-9-]{20,}' "0" "$content" "$location"
+  check_rule "BLOCK" "aws-access-key" 'AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}' "0" "$content" "$location"
+  check_rule "BLOCK" "private-key" '-----BEGIN ([A-Z ]+ )?PRIVATE KEY-----' "0" "$content" "$location"
+  check_rule "BLOCK" "secret-assignment" '(secret|token|password|passwd|api[_-]?key|bearer)[A-Za-z0-9_]*[[:space:]]*[:=][[:space:]]*"?'"'"'?[A-Za-z0-9+/=_-]{16,}' "1" "$content" "$location"
+
+  if [ "$tier" = "both" ]; then
+    check_ip_rule "$content" "$location"
+    check_home_path_rule "$content" "$location"
+    check_rule "WARN" "mdns-local" '[A-Za-z0-9-]+\.local\b' "0" "$content" "$location"
+    check_email_rule "$content" "$location"
+  fi
+}
+
+# ── Unified-diff parsing (shared by --staged and --range) ──────────────────
+# scan_diff_stream <tier> — reads a `git diff -U0` stream on stdin, tracks
+# current file + line number from the hunk headers, and scans every added
+# (+) line. Deleted files (+++ /dev/null) are skipped (nothing added).
+scan_diff_stream() {
+  local tier="$1"
+  local current_file="" current_line=0 skip_file=1
+  local diffline
+  while IFS= read -r diffline || [ -n "$diffline" ]; do
+    case "$diffline" in
+      "+++ "*)
+        local f="${diffline#+++ }"
+        if [ "$f" = "/dev/null" ]; then
+          skip_file=1
+          current_file=""
+        else
+          current_file="${f#b/}"
+          skip_file=0
+        fi
+        ;;
+      "@@ "*)
+        local hunk="${diffline#@@ }"
+        hunk="${hunk%% @@*}"
+        local plus="${hunk#*+}"
+        current_line="${plus%%,*}"
+        ;;
+      +*)
+        if [ "$skip_file" -eq 0 ] && [ -n "$current_file" ]; then
+          local content="${diffline#+}"
+          scan_line "$content" "${current_file}:${current_line}" "$tier"
+          current_line=$((current_line + 1))
+        fi
+        ;;
+      *) : ;;
+    esac
+  done
+}
+
+# ── blob-stdin: raw content on stdin, tracking `commit <sha>` headers ──────
+scan_blob_stdin() {
+  local tier="$1"
+  local current_commit="stdin"
+  local line
+  while IFS= read -r line || [ -n "$line" ]; do
+    case "$line" in
+      commit\ *)
+        current_commit="commit ${line#commit }"
+        # Trim any trailing " (something)" merge annotation down to the sha token.
+        current_commit="commit $(printf '%s' "${current_commit#commit }" | awk '{print $1}')"
+        ;;
+      "+++ "*|"---"*|"@@ "*) : ;;  # header noise, not content
+      +*)
+        local content="${line#+}"
+        scan_line "$content" "$current_commit" "$tier"
+        ;;
+      *) : ;;
+    esac
+  done
+}
+
+# ── Mode dispatch ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+MODE="${1:-}"
+[ "$#" -gt 0 ] && shift
+
+case "$MODE" in
+  --staged)
+    # Process substitution, NOT a pipe: scan_diff_stream mutates global
+    # FOUND/FOUND_RULES, which must survive in THIS shell, not a pipeline
+    # subshell (`cmd | scan_diff_stream` would run the function in a
+    # subshell and silently lose every finding).
+    scan_diff_stream "both" < <(git diff --cached -U0 --no-color 2>/dev/null)
+    ;;
+  --message)
+    MSG_FILE="${1:-}"
+    if [ -z "$MSG_FILE" ] || [ ! -f "$MSG_FILE" ]; then
+      echo "vibe-content-scan.sh --message: missing or unreadable message file '$MSG_FILE'" >&2
+      exit 1
+    fi
+    while IFS= read -r line || [ -n "$line" ]; do
+      scan_line "$line" "message" "both"
+    done < "$MSG_FILE"
+    ;;
+  --range)
+    A="${1:-}"; B="${2:-}"
+    if [ -z "$A" ] || [ -z "$B" ]; then
+      echo "vibe-content-scan.sh --range: needs two revisions" >&2
+      exit 1
+    fi
+    scan_diff_stream "block" < <(git diff -U0 --no-color "$A" "$B" 2>/dev/null)
+    ;;
+  --blob-stdin)
+    TIER="both"
+    if [ "${1:-}" = "--tier" ] && [ "${2:-}" = "block" ]; then
+      TIER="block"
+    fi
+    scan_blob_stdin "$TIER"
+    ;;
+  *)
+    echo "vibe-content-scan.sh: unknown mode '$MODE' (expected --staged|--message|--range|--blob-stdin)" >&2
+    exit 1
+    ;;
+esac
+
+# ── Decide exit code ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+if [ "$GUARD_OVERRIDE" -eq 1 ]; then
+  if [ "$FOUND" -eq 1 ]; then
+    rules_list="${FOUND_RULES[*]}"
+    echo "vibe-content-scan.sh: OVERRIDE (VIBE_CONTENT_GUARD=off / VIBE_ALLOW_COMMIT=1) — skipped enforcement for: ${rules_list// /, }" >&2
+  fi
+  exit 0
+fi
+
+if [ "$FOUND" -eq 1 ]; then
+  exit 1
+fi
+exit 0

+# Sync the content-guard git hooks (task_019) into $DEST_ROOT/vibe-git-hooks/
+# (chmod +x on the scanner + three wrappers) and point git's global
+# core.hooksPath at that directory, so pre-commit/commit-msg/pre-push fire
+# for every repo the container touches, INCLUDING rw /repos/* shared repos
+# and (in the gardener) brain2 (core.hooksPath is --global, same scope as
+# ensure_shared_repos_safe_directory's safe.directory entries above — see
+# .vs/spec.md's "Note on core.hooksPath global scope"). Idempotent: re-runs
+# just re-copy + re-chmod + re-set the same config value. Unlike commands/
+# agents, hook files under vibe-git-hooks/ are enforcement code, not
+# user-editable content, so there is no "leave user edits alone" carve-out.
+install_git_hooks() {
+  local src="$SRC_ROOT/git-hooks"
+  local dest="$DEST_ROOT/vibe-git-hooks"
+
+  [ -d "$src" ] || return 0
+  mkdir -p "$dest"
+
+  local file name
+  for file in "$src"/*; do
+    [ -f "$file" ] || continue
+    name=$(basename "$file")
+    cp -f "$file" "$dest/$name"
+    chmod +x "$dest/$name"
+  done
+
+  git config --global core.hooksPath "$dest"
+}
+
 install_dir agents
 install_dir commands
 install_hooks
+install_git_hooks
 install_claude_md_fragments
 install_brain2_skills
 check_superpowers

 CREDENTIAL_HELPER = REPO / "devcontainer" / "credential-helper.sh"
 SETUP_GIT_SH = REPO / "devcontainer" / "setup-git.sh"

+def test_task019_ac1_staged_ghp_token_blocks() -> None:
+    """AC1: vibe-content-scan.sh --staged with runtime-built GHP token exits 1, emits BLOCK line."""
+    print("\n[task_019 AC1: staged GHP token blocks]")
+    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as td:
+        repo = Path(td) / "repo"
+        repo.mkdir()
+        run(["git", "init"], cwd=repo)
+        run(["git", "config", "user.email", "test@example.com"], cwd=repo)
+        run(["git", "config", "user.name", "Test User"], cwd=repo)
+
+        # Create a file with a runtime-constructed token (no literal secret in this code)
+        token = "ghp_" + ("A" * 36)
+        test_file = repo / "secret.txt"
+        test_file.write_text(f"My secret is {token}\n")
+        run(["git", "add", "secret.txt"], cwd=repo)
+
+        r = run(["bash", str(VIBE_CONTENT_SCANNER), "--staged"], cwd=repo)
+        check("[task_019 AC1] exit 1", r.returncode == 1, r.stderr[:200])
+        check("[task_019 AC1] BLOCK in stderr", "BLOCK" in r.stderr, r.stderr)
+        check("[task_019 AC1] github-pat rule named", "github-pat" in r.stderr, r.stderr)
+

+def test_task019_ac6_allowlist_suppresses_finding() -> None:
+    """AC6: .vibe-content-allow suppresses findings matching its regex."""
+    print("\n[task_019 AC6: allowlist suppresses]")
+    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as td:
+        repo = Path(td) / "repo"

+# ── Content-guard audit (task_019) ────────────────────────────────────────────
+# `vibe audit` is host-side and runs entirely against the CURRENT directory's
+# git repo — no container involved, mirroring `vibe repos`. It uses vibe's
+# OWN source copy of the scanner (DEVCONTAINER_DIR/git-hooks/, not the copy
+# installed into a container's ~/.claude/vibe-git-hooks/), since it operates
+# on the host machine's checkout, not inside a devcontainer.
+
+_audit_scanner_path() {
+  echo "$DEVCONTAINER_DIR/git-hooks/vibe-content-scan.sh"
+}
+
+_audit_require_repo() {
+  local scanner
+  scanner="$(_audit_scanner_path)"
+  if [ ! -x "$scanner" ]; then
+    echo "vibe audit: scanner not found at $scanner" >&2
+    exit 1
+  fi
+  if ! git rev-parse --show-toplevel >/dev/null 2>&1; then
+    echo "vibe audit: not inside a git repository" >&2
+    exit 1
+  fi
+}
+
+_audit_usage() {
+  cat <<'EOF'
+Usage: vibe audit [--history|--staged]
+
+  --history   (default) scan the full repo history, BOTH tiers - every
+              commit's added content (git log -p --all) plus every commit
+              message. Exits 1 only if a BLOCK-class finding is present;
+              WARN-only history exits 0 but the findings are still listed
+              (advisory - this is the Private->Public flip case a
+              forward-looking git-hook layer cannot retroactively cover).
+
+  --staged    scan the currently staged diff on demand (pre-commit
+              equivalent), outside of the git hook flow.
+
+Respects .vibe-content-allow and .vibe-content-guard-off in the repo root.
+Never rewrites history - reports only.
+EOF
+  exit 0
+}
+
+# _audit_staged — thin pass-through to `--staged`, printing the scanner's own
+# stderr findings and propagating its exit code as-is (no aggregation needed:
+# --staged already has the right both-tiers-exit-nonzero semantics).
+_audit_staged() {
+  _audit_require_repo
+  local scanner
+  scanner="$(_audit_scanner_path)"
+  if "$scanner" --staged; then
+    exit 0
+  else
+    exit 1
+  fi
+}
+
+# _audit_history — full-history scan, BOTH tiers, per component 7 of
+# .vs/spec.md. Two passes, each captured to a temp file (findings are on
+# stderr, tab-separated <CLASS>\t<location>\t<rule>\t<snippet>):
+#
+#   1. Content: `git log -p --all` piped through --blob-stdin (default tier
+#      "both"), which tracks `commit <sha>` headers itself and attributes
+#      each finding's location to that commit.
+#   2. Messages: `--message` doesn't know which commit it's scanning (its
+#      location is always the literal "message"), so this loop calls it
+#      once per commit and rewrites the location field to "commit <sha>"
+#      before appending - preserving --message's own both-tier + trailer-
+#      exemption logic without duplicating it.
+#
+# Audit's own exit code is computed HERE, independent of either scanner
+# invocation's exit code (which would return 1 on ANY finding, WARN
+# included): 1 iff a BLOCK-class line appears in the aggregate, 0 otherwise
+# (component 7: "WARN-only history exits 0 but still lists the WARN
+# findings"). Findings are grouped BLOCK-then-WARN in the printed report.
+_audit_history() {
+  _audit_require_repo
+  local scanner
+  scanner="$(_audit_scanner_path)"
+
+  local tmp_content tmp_messages tmp_msgfile
+  tmp_content="$(mktemp)"
+  tmp_messages="$(mktemp)"
+  tmp_msgfile="$(mktemp)"
+  # Register through the single EXIT-trap dispatcher (see "Exit-hook
+  # dispatcher" above) — never a raw `trap ... EXIT` here, which would
+  # silently replace whatever trap slot a later hook installs.
+  vibe_exit_hook_add "rm -f '$tmp_content' '$tmp_messages' '$tmp_msgfile'"
+
+  # Pass 1: full-history content, both tiers, commit-sha location tracking.
+  git log -p --no-color --all 2>/dev/null | "$scanner" --blob-stdin >/dev/null 2>"$tmp_content" || true
+
+  # Pass 2: every commit message, attributed to its own commit sha.
+  : > "$tmp_messages"
+  local sha
+  while IFS= read -r sha; do
+    [ -n "$sha" ] || continue
+    git log -1 --format=%B "$sha" > "$tmp_msgfile" 2>/dev/null || true
+    "$scanner" --message "$tmp_msgfile" 2>&1 1>/dev/null \
+      | awk -F'\t' -v sha="$sha" 'BEGIN{OFS="\t"} NF>=4{$2="commit " sha; print}' \
+      >> "$tmp_messages" || true
+  done < <(git log --all --format=%H 2>/dev/null)
+
+  local has_block=0 any=0
+  if awk -F'\t' '$1=="BLOCK"{f=1} END{exit !f}' "$tmp_content" "$tmp_messages" 2>/dev/null; then
+    has_block=1
+  fi
+
+  echo "vibe audit --history: full-history scan (content + commit messages, both tiers)"
+  if awk -F'\t' '$1=="BLOCK"{f=1} END{exit !f}' "$tmp_content" "$tmp_messages" 2>/dev/null; then
+    echo
+    echo "BLOCK:"
+    awk -F'\t' '$1=="BLOCK"' "$tmp_content" "$tmp_messages"
+    any=1
+  fi
+  if awk -F'\t' '$1=="WARN"{f=1} END{exit !f}' "$tmp_content" "$tmp_messages" 2>/dev/null; then
+    echo
+    echo "WARN (advisory - exit code unaffected):"
+    awk -F'\t' '$1=="WARN"' "$tmp_content" "$tmp_messages"
+    any=1
+  fi
+  if [ "$any" -eq 0 ]; then
+    echo "  clean - no findings across full history"
+  fi
+
+  if [ "$has_block" -eq 1 ]; then
+    exit 1
+  fi
+  exit 0
+}
+
+# audit_handle_subcommand <args...> — top-level dispatcher for `vibe audit`,
+# invoked from its own dispatch block (mirrors `learn`'s and `repos`', see
+# the block immediately before parse_vibe_args below).
+audit_handle_subcommand() {
+  shift  # consume "audit"
+  local subcmd="${1:-}"
+  case "$subcmd" in
+    --history|"")
+      _audit_history
+      ;;
+    --staged)
+      _audit_staged
+      ;;
+    --help|-h)
+      _audit_usage
+      ;;
+    *)
+      echo "vibe audit: unknown option '$subcmd'" >&2
+      exit 1
+      ;;
+  esac
+}
+
 # ── Learning mount helper ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 
 # _build_override_config <workspace_abs_path> — collects the bind mounts that
@@ -2427,6 +2582,17 @@ if [ "${1:-}" = "repos" ]; then
   exit $?
 fi
 
+# ── Audit subcommand dispatch (task_019) ──────────────────────────────────────
+# Must be BEFORE the --* flag-parser loop — mirrors `learn`/`repos` above.
+# Host-side only: scans the CURRENT directory's git repo directly, no
+# container involved. Dispatches and exits; does NOT enter workspace
+# resolution, preflight, image build, GitHub setup, or container launch.
+if [ "${1:-}" = "audit" ]; then
+  audit_handle_subcommand "$@"
+  # audit_handle_subcommand's sub-functions always exit; this is a safety net.
+  exit $?
+fi
+

 # parse_vibe_args (defined above the VIBE_SOURCE_ONLY guard so smoke-test.py
 # can source-test it) accepts flags and the project positional in any order.

++## 2026-07-11
++
++- [x] **shared-repos cycle 1: registry + declaration + read-only mounts + honest header** — task_017, first of 4 planned `/vs` cycles (rw lock lands C2, `/repo` claim/handoff + CLAUDE.md seam fragment C3, per-repo credential routing via `useHttpPath` C4). The problem: a public `<x>andeye` project sometimes needs live cross-repo development against a private repo (e.g. `andeyePro/andeyePro`) without either repo's blast radius widening. Mechanics: a project commits `.vibe-repos` (`owner/repo [ro|rw]` lines, charset-validated, comments/blanks allowed — deliberately NOT gitignored, since declaring WHAT a project uses is meant to travel with it); each machine separately registers WHERE that repo actually lives via `vibe repos add <owner/repo> [path]` into `~/.vibe/repos` (`slug=path`, chmod 600 like `~/.vibe/tokens`, which now also serves shared-repo PATs keyed by slug — reusing `lookup_token`/`setup_token` as-is). New `vibe repos` subcommand (`add` / `remove [--purge]` / `list`) dispatches in its own pre-`parse_vibe_args` block, mirroring `learn`'s exact placement, so `vibe repos add owner/repo` can never be swallowed by the positional-project-name catch-all. `shared_repos_scan` is the single classification pass (used by `list`, the launch header, the runtime manifest, AND `_build_override_config`'s mount-triple assembly, so none of the four can ever disagree): it emits `M`/`B`/`N` per declared slug — mounted, registered-but-broken-with-reason, or never-registered — and the header renders the never-registered case as TOTAL SILENCE (the community-contributor property: someone without the private repo sees nothing) versus a loud named warning for anything registered-but-broken (missing checkout, missing token, reserved dot-prefixed basename, basename collision). Every shared repo contributes TWO bind mounts from this cycle onward: the checkout itself (hard-pinned read-only in C1 — the declaration's `rw` field already parses so C2's lock logic has somewhere to read from, it just isn't wired to the actual bind flag yet) and its `.vibe-signals/` sidecar, always read-write even on a read-only code mount — that's what will let an ro session file an rw claim once C3 lands `/repo claim`. The sidecar directory is created host-side (`shared_repo_ensure_signals`, guarded/idempotent) at both `vibe repos add` time and defensively at mount assembly, specifically so Docker never auto-vivifies it as a root-owned bind target. A runtime manifest (`/workspace/.vibe/shared-repos.manifest`, one `name mode slug` line per mount) is written strictly before `devcontainer up` so `install-claude-extras.sh` can register `git config --global --add safe.directory /repos/<name>` for each one in the SAME launch — critical for the relaunch immediately after `vibe repos add`. `GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0` ships as a plain `devcontainer.json` containerEnv/remoteEnv constant (applied container-wide as a safe simplification — it's a read-path optimisation toggle, never a correctness concern). `ensure_project_gitignore`'s managed block gains `.vibe-signals/` (NOT `.vibe-repos`, which stays committed by design); `shared_repo_ensure_signals` is gitignore owner #2, for shared checkouts that aren't vibe projects themselves. shellcheck clean (15 files, two SC2318/SC2034 fixes during dev); full pre-existing smoke suite green (1080/1080, no regressions — the Tester's task_017 checks land in a later cycle per `/vs`'s Generator/Tester independence). README gains a Shared repos bullet + `~/.vibe/repos` host-state row + the `vibe repos add` usage line.
++
+ ## 2026-07-10
+ 
+ - [x] **`/vs --panel [N]`: blind review panel + sycophancy check** — ports the two agent-review-panel mechanisms the 2026-07 harness-landscape audit flagged as `/vs`'s clearest QA gap. N panellists (default 3, odd, Sonnet — deliberately not the upstream all-Opus: the mechanism's value is independence, not depth) dispatch as read-only `code-reviewer` agents in one concurrent batch with byte-identical briefs (no assigned personas — differentiation must emerge), each blind to the others' verdicts. The Evaluator then runs a mandatory correlated-agreement check: unanimous near-identical rationales = LOW-information consensus (logged as a weakness, optional single Opus depth-probe on high-blast-radius diffs); independent convergence = earned confidence; splits get written chair adjudication, and an unrefuted BLOCKING dissent from any one panellist blocks a pass regardless of majority. Composes with `--fuzzy` (replaces the single Reviewer) and rigorous mode (adds judgment beside the mechanical gate, which still governs); orthogonal to `--verbosity`/`--plain`/`--cost` (`role: "panel_reviewer"`). New vs.md § Step 5c + Flags + Model economy + Rules + artifact paths (`cycle-N/panel/`); 24 smoke checks guard the load-bearing properties. Authored chair-side per the /vss planner's hybrid mode; independently reviewed pre-commit by a blind read-only Sonnet reviewer, whose 7 findings (Step 6 never mandated reading the panel files; 5b/5c double-dispatch ambiguity; flow diagram omission; unvalidated N; overclaimed byte-identity; unannotated divergence from upstream's 4-6 panellists; one non-discriminating smoke check) were all fixed pre-commit.

++# Shared-repos git ergonomics (AC6, task_017 cycle 1): the runtime manifest
++# at /workspace/.vibe/shared-repos.manifest (one "name mode slug" line per
++# mounted shared repo, written by the `vibe` launcher STRICTLY BEFORE
++# `devcontainer up` in THIS SAME launch — see shared_repos_manifest_lines /
++# the SHARED_REPOS_MANIFEST write in the launcher) lists what's bind-mounted
++# at /repos/<name>. There's no pre-existing safe.directory mechanism in this
++# codebase to mirror — /workspace itself has never needed one, since its
++# ownership maps cleanly on the primary Mac platform. A shared-repo checkout
++# gets one because it's a bind mount of a DIFFERENT host path owned by the
++# same invoking user, and git's dubious-ownership check can still trip on
++# the uid mapping a fresh mount presents inside the container. Runs on every
++# container start; adds ONE literal per-repo `--add`-style entry (no `*`
++# wildcard — a wildcard would trust every future bind, not just today's
++# declared set) and de-duplicates first, since `git config --add` is not
++# itself idempotent (it would append a second identical line on every
++# restart otherwise). Reads the mount root from ${VIBE_REPOS_DIR:-/repos}
++# (not a hardcoded /repos) so a smoke fixture can point this at a temp tree
++# instead of the real container mount point.
++#
++# GIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS=0 guidance (also AC6): shipped as a plain, constant
++# containerEnv/remoteEnv entry in devcontainer.json rather than computed
++# here — it's a fixed value, not derived from the manifest, and every other
++# constant in this container (NODE_OPTIONS, CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR, ...) is
++# already set that way. Applied container-wide rather than scoped to just
++# the ro shared checkouts: git optional locks are a read-path optimisation,
++# never a correctness requirement, so disabling them everywhere is a safe
++# simplification instead of per-repo plumbing that would need a matching
++# ro/rw distinction of its own.
++ensure_shared_repos_safe_directory() {
++  local manifest="${VIBE_SHARED_REPOS_MANIFEST:-/workspace/.vibe/shared-repos.manifest}"
++  [ -f "$manifest" ] || return 0
++  local repos_root="${VIBE_REPOS_DIR:-/repos}"
++
++  # Manifest lines are "name mode slug" (AC5); only the basename is needed
++  # here, but mode/slug must still be consumed positionally so `name` gets
++  # just the first field, not the whole line.
++  local name dir mode slug
++  # shellcheck disable=SC2034  # mode/slug consumed positionally, not used
++  while read -r name mode slug; do
++    [ -n "$name" ] || continue
++    dir="$repos_root/$name"
++    if ! git config --global --get-all safe.directory 2>/dev/null | grep -qxF "$dir"; then
++      git config --global --add safe.directory "$dir"
++    fi
++  done < "$manifest"
++}

++# remove_token <repo> — deletes the stored PAT for <repo>, if any. Mirrors
++# save_token's grep-filter-then-rewrite pattern but drops the line instead of
++# replacing it. No-op (not an error) when TOKENS_FILE is missing or the key

++# ── Shared-repos helpers (task_017 cycle 1) ───────────────────────────────────
++# Declaration file: <project>/.vibe-repos, COMMITTED (one `<owner>/<repo>
++# <ro|rw>` line per repo, mode optional/default ro). Machine registry:
++# ~/.vibe/repos (REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE, `slug=path` lines, chmod 600). Every
++# helper here is defined above the VIBE_SOURCE_ONLY guard so smoke-test.py
++# can unit-test them by sourcing the launcher directly. All read paths follow
++# the lookup_token / auto_resume_field fail-safe discipline: a missing file,
++# an unmatched key, or a malformed value echoes NOTHING rather than raising
++# an error — callers treat empty output as "not configured", never as a bug.
++
++# is_valid_repo_slug <slug> — true iff slug is exactly `owner/repo` in the
++# charset [A-Za-z0-9._-]+/[A-Za-z0-9._-]+ (one slash, no path traversal, no
++# shell metacharacters). Shared by shared_repos_parse (reading the committed
++# declaration file) and `vibe repos add` (reading a CLI arg) so a hand-edited
++# file and the CLI enforce the identical rule.
++is_valid_repo_slug() {
++  [[ "${1:-}" =~ ^[A-Za-z0-9._-]+/[A-Za-z0-9._-]+$ ]]
++}
++
++# shared_repo_basename <slug> — echoes the mount-point basename: the part of
++# slug after the last '/'. Pure string op, no I/O.
++shared_repo_basename() {
++  printf '%s' "${1##*/}"
++}
++
++# shared_repo_env_name <slug> — echoes the full per-repo token env var name:
++# VIBE_SHARED_TOKEN_<SANITISED>, sanitisation = uppercase then every
++# non-alphanumeric character (including slug's own '/') becomes '_'. E.g.
++# andeyePro/andeyePro -> VIBE_SHARED_TOKEN_ANDEYEPRO_ANDEYEPRO. Pure string
++# transform; collision detection between two configured slugs sanitising to
++# the same name is `vibe repos add`'s job (see _repos_add below), not this
++# helper's.
++shared_repo_env_name() {
++  local upper
++  upper=$(printf '%s' "$1" | tr '[:lower:]' '[:upper:]')
++  printf 'VIBE_SHARED_TOKEN_%s' "$(printf '%s' "$upper" | tr -c 'A-Z0-9' '_')"
++}
++
++# shared_repos_parse <file> — reads a .vibe-repos declaration file, echoing
++# one "slug mode" line per VALID entry (mode is always "ro" or "rw", defaulted
++# to "ro" when the file omits it). Comments (lines starting with `#`, after
++# whitespace-trimming) and blank lines are skipped silently. A malformed line
++# (bad slug charset, bad mode, or unexpected trailing content) is skipped
++# with a one-line stderr warning naming the line number and offending text —
++# never aborts the read, so one bad hand-edited line can't hide every other
++# declaration. Missing file echoes nothing (fail-safe). `read`'s own
++# whitespace-splitting does the trimming; no sed/awk needed.
++shared_repos_parse() {
++  local file="$1"
++  [ -f "$file" ] || return 0
++  local lineno=0 raw slug mode extra
++  while IFS= read -r raw || [ -n "$raw" ]; do
++    lineno=$((lineno + 1))
++    slug="" mode="" extra=""
++    read -r slug mode extra <<< "$raw"
++    case "$slug" in
++      ''|'#'*) continue ;;  # blank or (whitespace-then-)comment line
++    esac
++    if ! is_valid_repo_slug "$slug"; then
++      echo "vibe: .vibe-repos:${lineno}: malformed slug '${slug}' — skipped" >&2
++      continue
++    fi
++    mode="${mode:-ro}"
++    case "$mode" in
++      ro|rw) ;;
++      *)
++        echo "vibe: .vibe-repos:${lineno}: invalid mode '${mode}' for '${slug}' — skipped" >&2
++        continue
++        ;;
++    esac
++    if [ -n "$extra" ]; then
++      echo "vibe: .vibe-repos:${lineno}: unexpected content after mode for '${slug}' — skipped" >&2
++      continue
++    fi
++    echo "$slug $mode"
++  done < "$file"
++}
++
++# repos_registry_lookup <slug> — echoes the registered local checkout path
++# for <slug> from REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE (`slug=path` lines), or nothing if
++# unregistered, the file is missing, or the resolved path fails validation
++# (contains a newline or a double-quote, or isn't absolute — a hand-trampled
++# registry line silently fails to resolve rather than propagating garbage
++# into a mount path). Mirrors lookup_token's `cut -d= -f2-` (not `-f2`) so a
++# path containing '=' is returned whole.
++repos_registry_lookup() {
++  local slug="$1"
++  [ -f "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" ] || return 0
++  is_valid_repo_slug "$slug" || return 0
++  local path
++  path=$(grep "^${slug}=" "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" 2>/dev/null | tail -1 | cut -d= -f2-) || return 0
++  [ -z "$path" ] && return 0
++  case "$path" in
++    *$'\n'*|*'"'*) return 0 ;;
++  esac
++  case "$path" in
++    /*) ;;
++    *) return 0 ;;
++  esac
++  printf '%s' "$path"
++}
++
++# repos_registry_save <slug> <path> — writes/updates the `slug=path` entry in
++# REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE (chmod 600, like TOKENS_FILE). Mirrors save_token's
++# grep-filter-then-rewrite pattern against a different file.
++repos_registry_save() {
++  local slug="$1" path="$2"
++  mkdir -p "$(dirname "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE")"
++  touch "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++  local tmp
++  tmp=$(mktemp)
++  grep -v "^${slug}=" "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" > "$tmp" || true
++  echo "${slug}=${path}" >> "$tmp"
++  mv "$tmp" "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++  chmod 600 "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++}
++
++# repos_registry_remove <slug> — drops <slug>'s entry from REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE
++# (used by `vibe repos remove --purge`). No-op when the file or the key is
++# absent.
++repos_registry_remove() {
++  local slug="$1"
++  [ -f "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" ] || return 0
++  local tmp
++  tmp=$(mktemp)
++  grep -v "^${slug}=" "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" > "$tmp" || true
++  mv "$tmp" "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++  chmod 600 "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++}
++
++# shared_repo_ensure_signals <checkout> — idempotently ensures the
++# .vibe-signals/ sidecar exists under <checkout> (host-side `mkdir -p`, so
++# it's owned by the invoking user rather than whatever uid Docker's bind
++# auto-vivification would pick) AND that .vibe-signals/ is gitignored in that
++# checkout's OWN .gitignore — a second, independent owner from
++# ensure_project_gitignore's managed block (install-claude-extras.sh), needed
++# because a shared checkout may not itself be a vibe project and may never
++# have launched vibe. Called from BOTH `vibe repos add` (registration time,
++# see _repos_add) and shared_repos_scan (defensively, before any bind
++# referencing the sidecar) — both call sites are guarded/idempotent, so
++# calling this twice (or a hundred times) across a launch is harmless.
++# Never aborts the caller on an unwritable checkout (read-only mount,
++# offline network volume, etc): returns 1 so the caller can demote the repo
++# to registered-but-broken (reason "sidecar unwritable") instead of tripping
++# `set -e`. Returns 0 on success.
++shared_repo_ensure_signals() {
++  local checkout="$1" sidecar gitignore
++  [ -n "$checkout" ] || return 1
++  sidecar="$checkout/.vibe-signals"
++  mkdir -p "$sidecar" 2>/dev/null || return 1
++  [ -w "$sidecar" ] || return 1
++
++  gitignore="$checkout/.gitignore"
++  if [ -f "$gitignore" ]; then
++    if ! grep -qxF ".vibe-signals/" "$gitignore" 2>/dev/null; then
++      echo ".vibe-signals/" >> "$gitignore" 2>/dev/null || return 1
++    fi
++  else
++    echo ".vibe-signals/" > "$gitignore" 2>/dev/null || return 1
++  fi
++  return 0
++}
++
++# shared_repos_scan <workspace> — the SINGLE classification pass shared by
++# `vibe repos list`, the launch header, the runtime manifest, and
++# _build_override_config's mount-triple assembly (deliberate: one code path
++# deciding what's mounted means the header can never disagree with what
++# actually got bind-mounted). Reads <workspace>/.vibe-repos via
++# shared_repos_parse and, for each validated (slug, mode) line, echoes
++# EXACTLY ONE of:
++#   M <name> <bindmode> <slug> <checkout>   — resolved & mounted
++#   B <slug> <reason...>                    — registered but broken
++#   N <slug>                                — never registered on this machine
++# The M/B/N split is what lets AC4's header distinguish "no registry entry"
++# (N — total silence, the community-contributor case) from "registry entry
++# broken" (B — loud warning) as two different branches below, not two
++# renderings of one branch. bindmode is hard-pinned "ro" in cycle 1
++# regardless of the declared mode (the mode field parses now so cycle 2's
++# rw-intent + lock logic has somewhere to read from; only cycle 2 wires it to
++# the actual bind flag). Side effect: a repo that reaches shared_repo_ensure_
++# signals gets its sidecar mkdir'd/gitignored here; a failure there demotes
++# it to B ("sidecar unwritable") rather than aborting — sibling repos are
++# still processed (never a hard failure partway through the scan).
++shared_repos_scan() {
++  local workspace="$1"
++  local decl="$workspace/.vibe-repos"
++  local seen_names="" slug mode name path bindmode
++
++  while read -r slug mode; do
++    [ -n "$slug" ] || continue
++
++    name="$(shared_repo_basename "$slug")"
++
++    # Reserved dot-prefixed basenames: the .vibe-signals sidecar namespace
++    # lives beside repo mounts, so a repo named e.g. `.foo` would collide
++    # with it. `vibe repos add` rejects these at registration; this is the
++    # defensive re-check for a hand-edited .vibe-repos that slipped one in.
++    case "$name" in
++      .*)
++        echo "vibe: shared repo '$slug': mount skipped - basenames beginning with '.' are reserved" >&2
++        echo "B $slug reserved dot-prefixed name '$name'"
++        continue
++        ;;
++    esac
++
++    # Basename collision: only matters against a name that ALREADY resolved
++    # to a real mount (see the `seen_names` update at the bottom) — a name
++    # clash against a repo that itself never mounts isn't a real conflict.
++    if printf '%s\n' "$seen_names" | grep -qxF "$name"; then
++      echo "B $slug basename '$name' collides with another declared repo"
++      continue
++    fi
++
++    path="$(repos_registry_lookup "$slug")"
++    if [ -z "$path" ]; then
++      echo "N $slug"
++      continue
++    fi
++
++    if [ ! -e "$path/.git" ]; then
++      echo "B $slug path missing or not a git checkout ($path)"
++      continue
++    fi
++
++    if [ -z "$(lookup_token "$slug")" ]; then
++      echo "B $slug no token configured (run: vibe repos add $slug)"
++      continue
++    fi
++
++    if ! shared_repo_ensure_signals "$path"; then
++      echo "B $slug sidecar unwritable ($path/.vibe-signals)"
++      continue
++    fi
++
++    seen_names="$seen_names
++$name"
++    bindmode="ro"  # cycle-1 hard-pin; rw arrives in cycle 2 via the lock
++    echo "M $name $bindmode $slug $path"
++  done < <(shared_repos_parse "$decl")
++}
++
++# shared_repos_manifest_lines <scan_output> — pure filter: given
++# shared_repos_scan's stdout, echoes the AC5 runtime-manifest lines ("name
++# mode slug", one per MOUNTED repo). No I/O — the caller redirects this to
++# the manifest file.
++shared_repos_manifest_lines() {
++  local scan="$1" scan_line name bindmode slug rest
++  while IFS= read -r scan_line; do
++    case "$scan_line" in
++      M\ *)
++        read -r name bindmode slug rest <<< "${scan_line#M }"
++        printf '%s %s %s\n' "$name" "$bindmode" "$slug"
++        ;;
++    esac
++  done <<< "$scan"
++}
++
++# ── Shared-repos subcommand internals (`vibe repos ...`) ─────────────────────
++# Operates on the CURRENT project directory via `pwd`, mirroring the learning
++# subcommand's `_learning_exclude_project` (not $WORKSPACE, which only exists
++# after the full launch flow resolves it — these subcommands dispatch and
++# exit before that point, see the dispatch block below).
++
++_repos_usage() {
++  echo "Usage: vibe repos add <owner/repo> [path]" >&2
++  echo "       vibe repos remove <owner/repo> [--purge]" >&2
++  echo "       vibe repos list" >&2
++  exit 1
++}
++
++# _repos_add <slug> [path] — validates <slug>, resolves/validates the local
++# checkout path (prompts if omitted; must contain .git), rejects a reserved
++# dot-prefixed basename or a basename/token-env collision against any OTHER
++# already-registered slug, writes the registry entry, ensures the signals
++# sidecar (+ its gitignore) in the checkout, appends the declaration to this
++# project's .vibe-repos if not already present, and mints a token if none is
++# stored yet. Exits non-zero with a one-line reason on any validation
++# failure; exits 0 with a relaunch reminder on success.
++_repos_add() {
++  local slug="${1:-}" path_arg="${2:-}"
++
++  if [ -z "$slug" ]; then
++    _repos_usage
++  fi
++  if ! is_valid_repo_slug "$slug"; then
++    echo "vibe repos add: '$slug' is not a valid owner/repo slug" >&2
++    exit 1
++  fi
++
++  local name
++  name="$(shared_repo_basename "$slug")"
++  case "$name" in
++    .*)
++      echo "vibe repos add: repo basenames beginning with '.' are reserved (the .vibe-signals sidecar namespace lives beside repo mounts)" >&2
++      exit 1
++      ;;
++  esac
++
++  # Collision checks against every OTHER already-registered slug: same mount
++  # basename, or same sanitised token env name.
++  local env_name
++  env_name="$(shared_repo_env_name "$slug")"
++  if [ -f "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE" ]; then
++    local existing_slug other_name other_env
++    while IFS='=' read -r existing_slug _; do
++      [ -n "$existing_slug" ] || continue
++      [ "$existing_slug" = "$slug" ] && continue
++      other_name="$(shared_repo_basename "$existing_slug")"
++      if [ "$other_name" = "$name" ]; then
++        echo "vibe repos add: basename '$name' already used by registered repo '$existing_slug' — mount points must be unique" >&2
++        exit 1
++      fi
++      other_env="$(shared_repo_env_name "$existing_slug")"
++      if [ "$other_env" = "$env_name" ]; then
++        echo "vibe repos add: '$slug' sanitises to the same token env var ($env_name) as already-registered '$existing_slug'" >&2
++        exit 1
++      fi
++    done < "$REPOS_REGISTRY_FILE"
++  fi
++
++  # Resolve the local checkout path.
++  local path="$path_arg"
++  if [ -z "$path" ]; then
++    read -rp "  Local path for $slug: " path
++  fi
++  case "$path" in
++    /*) ;;
++    *) path="$(cd "$path" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P)" || path="" ;;
++  esac
++  if [ -z "$path" ] || [ ! -d "$path" ]; then
++    echo "vibe repos add: '${path_arg:-$path}' is not a directory" >&2
++    exit 1
++  fi
++  if [ ! -e "$path/.git" ]; then
++    echo "vibe repos add: '$path' has no .git — point at an existing local checkout of $slug" >&2
++    echo "    (vibe repos add doesn't clone; if you don't have it yet: git clone https://github.com/$slug.git)" >&2
++    exit 1
++  fi
++
++  repos_registry_save "$slug" "$path"
++
++  if ! shared_repo_ensure_signals "$path"; then
++    echo "  ⚠ could not create $path/.vibe-signals (unwritable checkout?) — will show as BROKEN until fixed" >&2
++  fi
++
++  _vibe_repos_decl_append "$(pwd -P)/.vibe-repos" "$slug" "ro"
++
++  if [ -z "$(lookup_token "$slug")" ]; then
++    setup_token "$slug"
++  fi
++
++  echo "  ✓ $slug registered at $path and declared in .vibe-repos"
++  echo "    Relaunch (vibe) for the mount to take effect."
++  exit 0
++}
++
++# _vibe_repos_decl_has <file> <slug> — true iff <slug> is already declared
++# (any mode) in <file>, per shared_repos_parse's validated view.
++_vibe_repos_decl_has() {
++  local file="$1" slug="$2"
++  shared_repos_parse "$file" 2>/dev/null | cut -d' ' -f1 | grep -qxF "$slug"
++}
++
++# _vibe_repos_decl_append <file> <slug> <mode> — appends "<slug> <mode>" as a
++# new line (creating the file if absent). No-op if <slug> is already
++# declared (any mode) — see _vibe_repos_decl_has.
++_vibe_repos_decl_append() {
++  local file="$1" slug="$2" mode="$3"
++  _vibe_repos_decl_has "$file" "$slug" && return 0
++  printf '%s %s\n' "$slug" "$mode" >> "$file"
++}
++
++# _vibe_repos_decl_remove <file> <slug> — removes the line(s) declaring
++# <slug> from <file>, preserving every other line (comments, blanks, other
++# entries) untouched. No-op if the file or the slug isn't present.
++_vibe_repos_decl_remove() {
++  local file="$1" slug="$2"
++  [ -f "$file" ] || return 0
++  local tmp
++  tmp=$(mktemp)
++  grep -v -E "^${slug}([[:space:]]|\$)" "$file" > "$tmp" || true
++  mv "$tmp" "$file"
++}
++
++# _repos_remove <slug> [--purge] — removes <slug>'s declaration line from
++# this project's .vibe-repos (registry entry retained by default — other
++# projects may use it). --purge also drops the machine registry entry and,
++# if a token is stored, offers to delete it too. Exits non-zero with a
++# one-line reason on validation failure; exits 0 on success.
++_repos_remove() {
++  local slug="${1:-}" purge=""
++  if [ -z "$slug" ]; then
++    _repos_usage
++  fi
++  shift
++  case "${1:-}" in
++    --purge) purge=1 ;;
++    "") ;;
++    *)
++      echo "vibe repos remove: unknown option '$1'" >&2
++      exit 1
++      ;;
++  esac
++  if ! is_valid_repo_slug "$slug"; then
++    echo "vibe repos remove: '$slug' is not a valid owner/repo slug" >&2
++    exit 1
++  fi
++
++  local decl
++  decl="$(pwd -P)/.vibe-repos"
++  if ! _vibe_repos_decl_has "$decl" "$slug"; then
++    echo "vibe repos remove: '$slug' is not declared in this project's .vibe-repos" >&2
++    exit 1
++  fi
++  _vibe_repos_decl_remove "$decl" "$slug"
++  echo "  ✓ $slug removed from this project's .vibe-repos"
++
++  if [ -n "$purge" ]; then
++    repos_registry_remove "$slug"
++    echo "  ✓ $slug removed from the machine registry (~/.vibe/repos)"
++    if [ -n "$(lookup_token "$slug")" ]; then
++      if ask_yes_no "Also delete the stored token for $slug?" n; then
++        remove_token "$slug"
++        echo "  ✓ token deleted"
++      fi
++    fi
++  fi
++
++  echo "    Relaunch (vibe) for the change to take effect."
++  exit 0
++}
++
++# _repos_list — shows every repo declared in this project's .vibe-repos with
++# its resolution status: "mounted <ro|rw> at /repos/<name>", "BROKEN:
++# <reason>", or "not configured on this machine" — driven entirely by
++# shared_repos_scan's M/B/N tags (see its comment) so list can never disagree
++# with what a launch would actually mount. Always exits 0 (listing has no
++# validation-failure mode).
++_repos_list() {
++  local workspace decl
++  workspace="$(pwd -P)"
++  decl="$workspace/.vibe-repos"
++  if [ ! -f "$decl" ]; then
++    echo "  No .vibe-repos declaration in this project."
++    exit 0
++  fi
++
++  local scan_line found=0 name mode slug path reason
++  while IFS= read -r scan_line; do
++    case "$scan_line" in
++      M\ *)
++        read -r name mode slug path <<< "${scan_line#M }"
++        echo "  $slug - mounted $mode at /repos/$name"
++        found=1
++        ;;
++      B\ *)
++        read -r slug reason <<< "${scan_line#B }"
++        echo "  $slug - BROKEN: $reason"
++        found=1
++        ;;
++      N\ *)
++        read -r slug <<< "${scan_line#N }"
++        echo "  $slug - not configured on this machine"
++        found=1
++        ;;
++    esac
++  done < <(shared_repos_scan "$workspace")
++
++  [ "$found" -eq 1 ] || echo "  .vibe-repos declares nothing (every line was blank, a comment, or malformed - see warnings above)."
++  exit 0
++}
++
++# repos_handle_subcommand <args...> — top-level dispatcher for `vibe repos`,
++# invoked from its own dispatch block (mirrors `learn`'s, see the block
++# immediately before parse_vibe_args below). Every branch below exits inside
++# the sub-function it calls; nothing here relies on its own return value.
++repos_handle_subcommand() {
++  shift  # consume "repos"
++  local subcmd="${1:-}"
++  case "$subcmd" in
++    add)
++      shift
++      _repos_add "$@"
++      ;;
++    remove)
++      shift
++      _repos_remove "$@"
++      ;;
++    list)
++      _repos_list
++      ;;
++    "")
++      _repos_usage
++      ;;
++    *)
++      echo "vibe repos: unknown subcommand '$subcmd'" >&2
++      exit 1
++      ;;
++  esac
++}

++  # Each resolved repo contributes TWO bind triples: the checkout itself
++  # (ro, hard-pinned in cycle 1 — rw arrives in cycle 2's lock) at

++  # idempotent — its side effects are real mkdir/gitignore writes, which
